256<h2 id="bodyTitle">

257Childhood Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment (PDQ®)–Patient Version</h2>

264

265 <h3>

266General Information About Childhood Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma</h3>

267

268 <div id="_1" class="pdq-sections">

269

270 <div id="_section_1" class="pdq-sections">

271<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

272<a href="/types/lymphoma/hp/child-nhl-treatment-pdq">

273Go to Health Professional Version</a>

274</div>

275<div class="key-points">

276<h3 id="_1_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

277Key Points</h3>

278<div id="_kp_section_1_1">

279<ul>

280<li>

281Childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma is a disease in which

282 malignant (cancer) cells form in the lymph system, which is a part of the body's immune system.</li>

283<li>

284There are three major types of childhood non-Hodgkin

285 lymphoma.<ul>

286<li>

287Aggressive mature B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphoma</li>

288<li>

289Lymphoblastic lymphoma</li>

290<li>

291Anaplastic large cell lymphoma</li>

292</ul>

293</li>

294<li>

295Some types of non-Hodgkin lymphoma are rare in children.</li>

296<li>

297Having a weakened immune system increases the risk of NHL in children.</li>

298<li>

299Signs of childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma include

300 breathing problems and swollen lymph nodes.</li>

301<li>

302Tests that examine the body and lymph system are used to diagnose childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</li>

303<li>

304A biopsy is done to diagnose childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</li>

305<li>

306Certain factors affect prognosis (chance

307 of recovery) and treatment options.</li>

308</ul>

309</div>

310</div>

311<section id="_2">

312<h3 id="_3" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

313Childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma is a disease in which

314 malignant (cancer) cells form in the lymph system, which is a part of the body's immune system.</h3>

315<p id="_6" tabindex="-1">

316The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

317immune system</a>

318 helps protect the body from <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45364&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045364&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

319infection</a>

320 and disease.</p>

321<p id="_471" tabindex="-1">

322The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=793442&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000793442&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

323lymph system</a>

324 is made up of the following:</p>

325<div class="pdq-content-list">

326<ul id="_107">

327<li>

328<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46305&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046305&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

329Lymph</a>

330: Colorless, watery <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

331fluid</a>

332 that travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

333lymph vessels</a>

334 and carries <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45765&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045765&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

335lymphocytes</a>

336 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45993&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045993&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

337(white blood cells)</a>

338. <div class="pdq-content-list">

339<ul id="_836">

340<li>

341<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44953&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044953&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

342B lymphocytes</a>

343, also called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45611&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045611&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

344B cells</a>

345, make <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44918&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044918&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

346antibodies</a>

347 to help fight infection. Most types of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

348non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

349 begin in B lymphocytes.</li>

350<li>

351<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

352T lymphocytes</a>

353, also called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

354T cells</a>

355, help B lymphocytes make the antibodies that help fight infection.</li>

356<li>

357<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44062&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044062&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

359, also called NK cells, attack cancer cells and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45941&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045941&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

360viruses.</a>

361</li>

363</div>

364</li>

371filter</a>

372 lymph and store white blood cells that help fight infection and disease. Lymph nodes are found along a network of lymph vessels throughout the body. Groups of lymph nodes are found in the neck, underarm, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46288&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046288&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

421Enlarge</a>

422<img id="_195" alt="Lymph system; drawing shows the tonsils, thymus, spleen, bone marrow, lymph vessels, and lymph nodes. One inset shows the inside structure of a lymph node and the attached lymph vessels with arrows showing how the lymph (clear, watery fluid) moves into and out of the lymph node. Another inset shows a close up of bone marrow with blood cells." title="Lymph system; drawing shows the tonsils, thymus, spleen, bone marrow, lymph vessels, and lymph nodes. One inset shows the inside structure of a lymph node and the attached lymph vessels with arrows showing how the lymph (clear, watery fluid) moves into and out of the lymph node. Another inset shows a close up of bone marrow with blood cells." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/653807-750.jpg">

423<figcaption class="caption-container">

424The lymph system is part of the body's immune system and is made up of tissues and organs that help protect the body from infection and disease. These include the tonsils, thymus, spleen, bone marrow, lymph vessels, and lymph nodes. Lymph (clear, watery fluid) and lymphocytes (white blood cells) travel through the lymph vessels and into the lymph nodes where the lymphocytes destroy harmful substances. The lymph enters the bloodstream through a large vein near the heart.</figcaption>

425</figure>

426<p id="_427" tabindex="-1">

427 Lymph tissue is also found in other parts of the body such as the stomach, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44751&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044751&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

430brain,</a>

431 and skin.</p>

432<p id="_837" tabindex="-1">

433Non-Hodgkin <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45368&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045368&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

434lymphoma</a>

463<h3 id="_10" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

464There are three major types of childhood non-Hodgkin

465 lymphoma.</h3>

466<p id="_11" tabindex="-1">

467The type of lymphoma is determined by how the cells look

468 under a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

469microscope</a>

470. The three major types of childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma

471 are:</p>

472<section id="_376">

473<h4 id="_377" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

474Aggressive mature B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphoma</h4>

475<p id="_378" tabindex="-1">

476<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46053&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046053&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

477Aggressive</a>

478 mature B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphomas include:</p>

479<div class="pdq-content-list">

480<ul id="_368">

481<li>

482<strong>

483Burkitt lymphoma/leukemia:</strong>

484 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45203&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045203&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

485Burkitt lymphoma</a>

486 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=256548&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000256548&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

487Burkitt leukemia</a>

488 are different forms of the same disease. Burkitt lymphoma/leukemia is an aggressive (fast-growing) <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=407758&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000407758&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

489disorder</a>

490 of B lymphocytes that is most common in children and young adults. It may form in the abdomen, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=777073&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000777073&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

491Waldeyer's ring</a>

492, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46611&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046611&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

493testicles</a>

494, bone, bone marrow, skin, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46481&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046481&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

495central nervous system</a>

496 (CNS), or head and neck. Burkitt leukemia may start in the lymph nodes as Burkitt lymphoma and then spread to the blood and bone marrow, or it may start in the blood and bone marrow without forming in the lymph nodes first.<p id="_454" tabindex="-1">

497Both Burkitt leukemia and Burkitt lymphoma have been linked to infection with the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45684&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045684&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

498Epstein-Barr virus</a>

499 (EBV), although EBV infection is more likely to occur in patients in Africa than in the United States. Burkitt lymphoma/leukemia is more common in White people. Burkitt lymphoma/leukemia is <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

500diagnosed</a>

501 when a sample of tissue is checked and a certain change to the <em class="gene-name">

502MYC</em>

503 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45693&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045693&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

504gene</a>

505 is found.</p>

506</li>

507<li>

508<strong>

509<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=428286&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000428286&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

510Diffuse large B-cell lymphoma</a>

511:</strong>

512 Diffuse large B-cell lymphoma is the most common type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma. It is a type of B-cell non-Hodgkin lymphoma that grows quickly in the lymph nodes. The spleen, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46312&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046312&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

513liver</a>

514, bone marrow, or other organs are also often affected. Diffuse large B-cell lymphoma occurs more often in <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=776825&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000776825&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

515adolescents</a>

516 than in children.</li>

517<li>

518<strong>

519<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=777025&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000777025&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

520Primary mediastinal B-cell lymphoma</a>

521:</strong>

522 A type of lymphoma that develops from B cells in the mediastinum (the area between the lungs). It may spread to nearby organs including the lungs and the sac around the heart. It may also spread to lymph nodes and distant organs including the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46325&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046325&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

523kidneys</a>

524. Primary mediastinal B-cell lymphoma occurs more often in older adolescents than in children.</li>

528<section id="_379">

529<h4 id="_380" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

530Lymphoblastic lymphoma</h4>

531<p id="_381" tabindex="-1">

532<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=597158&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000597158&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

533Lymphoblastic lymphoma</a>

534 is a type of lymphoma that mainly affects T-cell lymphocytes. It usually forms in the mediastinum (the area between the lungs). This causes trouble breathing, wheezing, trouble swallowing, or swelling of the head and neck. It may spread to lymph nodes, bone, bone marrow, skin, the CNS, abdominal organs, and other areas. Lymphoblastic lymphoma is a lot like <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45586&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045586&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

535acute lymphoblastic leukemia</a>

536 (ALL).</p>

537</section>

538<section id="_382">

539<h4 id="_383" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

540Anaplastic large cell lymphoma</h4>

541<p id="_384" tabindex="-1">

542<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45552&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045552&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

543Anaplastic large cell lymphoma</a>

544 is a type of lymphoma that mainly affects T-cell lymphocytes. It usually forms in the lymph nodes, skin, or bone, and sometimes forms in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46189&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046189&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

545gastrointestinal tract</a>

546, lung, tissue that covers the lungs, and muscle. Patients with anaplastic large cell lymphoma have a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44958&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044958&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

547receptor</a>

548, called CD30, on the surface of their T cells. In many children, anaplastic large cell lymphoma is marked by changes in the <em class="gene-name">

549<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=721252&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000721252&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

550ALK</a>

551</em>

552 gene that makes a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

553protein</a>

554 called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=723339&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000723339&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

555anaplastic lymphoma kinase</a>

556. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

557pathologist</a>

558 checks for these cell and gene changes to help diagnose anaplastic large cell lymphoma.</p>

561<section id="_385">

562<h3 id="_386" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

563Some types of non-Hodgkin lymphoma are rare in children.</h3>

564<p id="_387" tabindex="-1">

565Some types of childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma are less common. These include:</p>

566<div class="pdq-content-list">

567<ul id="_388">

568<li>

569<strong>

570Pediatric-type <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=428287&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000428287&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

571follicular lymphoma</a>

572</strong>

573: In children, follicular lymphoma occurs mainly in males. It is more likely to be found in one area and does not spread to other places in the body. It usually forms in the tonsils and lymph nodes in the neck, but may also form in the testicles, kidney, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46189&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046189&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

574gastrointestinal tract</a>

575, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46196&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046196&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

576salivary gland</a>

577.</li>

578<li>

579<strong>

580<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=543124&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000543124&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

581Marginal zone lymphoma</a>

582</strong>

583: Marginal zone lymphoma is a type of lymphoma that tends to grow and spread slowly and is usually found at an early <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

584stage.</a>

585 It may be found in the lymph nodes or in areas outside the lymph nodes. Marginal zone lymphoma found outside the lymph nodes in children is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44437&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044437&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

586mucosa-associated lymphoid tissue (MALT) lymphoma</a>

587. MALT may be linked to <em>

588<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45706&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045706&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

589Helicobacter pylori</a>

590</em>

591 infection of the gastrointestinal tract and <em>

592<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=777077&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000777077&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

593Chlamydophila psittaci</a>

594</em>

595 infection of the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44197&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044197&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

596conjunctival membrane</a>

597 which lines the eye. Marginal zone lymphoma is rare in children but common in adults.</li>

598<li>

599<strong>

600<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45345&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045345&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

601Primary central nervous system (CNS) lymphoma</a>

602</strong>

603: Primary CNS lymphoma is extremely rare in children.</li>

604<li>

605<strong>

606<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=405873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000405873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

607Peripheral T-cell lymphoma</a>

608</strong>

609: Peripheral T-cell lymphoma is an aggressive (fast-growing) non-Hodgkin lymphoma that begins in mature T lymphocytes. Other types of peripheral T-cell lymphoma include mature T-cell/natural killer-cell lymphoma, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=539104&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000539104&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

610extranodal</a>

611 NK/T-cell lymphoma, and gamma-delta hepatosplenic T-cell lymphoma. Peripheral T-cell lymphoma is rare in children.</li>

612<li>

613<strong>

614<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46771&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046771&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

615Cutaneous T-cell lymphoma</a>

616</strong>

617: Cutaneous T-cell lymphoma begins in the skin and can cause the skin to thicken or form a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

618tumor</a>

619. It is very rare in children but is more common in adolescents and young adults. There are different types of cutaneous T-cell lymphoma, such as cutaneous anaplastic large cell lymphoma, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

620subcutaneous</a>

621 panniculitis-like T-cell lymphoma, gamma-delta T-cell lymphoma, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45794&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045794&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

622mycosis fungoides</a>

623. Mycosis fungoides rarely occurs in children and adolescents. </li>

624</ul>

625</div>

627<section id="_432">

628<h3 id="_433" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

629Having a weakened immune system increases the risk of NHL in children.</h3>

630<p id="_434" tabindex="-1">

631Anything that increases a person's risk of getting a disease is called a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

632risk factor</a>

633. Not every child with one or more of these risk factors will develop NHL, and it will develop in some children who don't have any known risk factors. Talk with your child's doctor if you think your child may be at risk. </p>

634<p id="_435" tabindex="-1">

635Some of the types of immune system problems that have been linked with a higher risk of childhood NHL include the following:</p>

636<div class="pdq-content-list">

637<ul id="_436">

638<li>

639Being infected with the Epstein-Barr virus or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44366&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044366&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

640human immunodeficiency virus</a>

641 (HIV).</li>

642<li>

643Having a weakened immune system after a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46631&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046631&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

644transplant</a>

645 or from <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=482419&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000482419&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

646medicines</a>

647 given after a transplant.</li>

648<li>

649Having certain <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45098&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045098&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

650inherited</a>

651 diseases (such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=794884&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000794884&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

652DNA repair defect syndromes</a>

653 which include <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270853&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270853&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

654ataxia-telangiectasia</a>

655, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=794882&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000794882&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

656Nijmegen breakage syndrome</a>

657, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=768575&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000768575&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

658constitutional</a>

659 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=789741&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000789741&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

660mismatch repair deficiency</a>

661).</li>

662<li>

663Past treatment for cancer.</li>

664</ul>

665</div>

666<p id="_448" tabindex="-1">

667If lymphoma or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45767&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045767&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

668lymphoproliferative disease</a>

669 is linked to a weakened immune system from certain inherited diseases, HIV infection, a transplant or medicines given after a transplant, the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

670condition</a>

671 is called lymphoproliferative disease associated with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46357&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046357&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

672immunodeficiency</a>

673. The different types of lymphoproliferative disease associated with immunodeficiency include:</p>

674<div class="pdq-content-list">

675<ul id="_449">

676<li>

677Lymphoproliferative disease associated with primary immunodeficiency.</li>

678<li>

679HIV-associated non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</li>

680<li>

681<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=468786&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000468786&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

682Post-transplant lymphoproliferative disease</a>

683.</li>

684<li>

685Lymphoproliferative disease from chemotherapy.</li>

686</ul>

690<h3 id="_15" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

691Signs of childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma include

692 breathing problems and swollen lymph nodes.</h3>

693<p id="_16" tabindex="-1">

694These and other <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

695signs</a>

696 may be caused by childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma or by other conditions. Check with a doctor if your child has any of the following:</p>

697<div class="pdq-content-list">

698<ul id="_17">

699<li>

700Trouble breathing.</li>

701<li>

702Wheezing.</li>

703<li>

704Coughing.</li>

705<li>

706 High-pitched breathing sounds.</li>

707<li>

708Swelling of the head, neck, upper body, or arms.</li>

709<li>

710Trouble swallowing.</li>

711<li>

712Painless swelling of the lymph nodes in the neck, underarm,

713 stomach, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46375&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046375&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

714groin</a>

715.</li>

716<li>

717Painless lump or swelling in a testicle.

718</li>

719<li>

720<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=450108&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000450108&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

721Fever</a>

722 for no known reason.</li>

723<li>

724Weight loss for no known reason.</li>

725<li>

726Drenching <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=454810&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000454810&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

727night sweats</a>

728.</li>

729<li>

730Pain or swelling in the abdomen.</li>

734<section id="_18">

735<h3 id="_19" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

736Tests that examine the body and lymph system are used to diagnose childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</h3>

737<p id="_20" tabindex="-1">

738In addition to asking about your child's <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=642019&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000642019&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

739personal</a>

740 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=642015&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000642015&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

741family health history</a>

742 and doing a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

743physical exam</a>

744, your child's doctor may perform the following tests and procedures:</p>

745<div class="pdq-content-list">

746<ul id="_21">

747<li>

748<strong>

749<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=304685&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000304685&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

750Blood chemistry studies</a>

751</strong>

752: A procedure in which a blood sample is checked to measure the amounts of certain substances released into the blood by organs and tissues in the body, including <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44338&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044338&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

753electrolytes</a>

754, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=354462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000354462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

755lactate dehydrogenase</a>

756 (LDH), <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=393536&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000393536&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

757uric acid</a>

758, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=572242&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000572242&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

759blood urea nitrogen</a>

760 (BUN), <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44337&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044337&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

761creatinine</a>

762, and liver function values. An unusual (higher or lower than normal) amount of a substance can be a sign of disease.</li>

763<li>

764<strong>

765<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=390293&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000390293&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

766Liver function tests</a>

767</strong>

768: A procedure in which a blood sample is checked to measure the amounts of certain substances released into the blood by the liver. A higher-than-normal amount of a substance can be a sign of cancer.</li>

769<li>

770<strong>

771<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

772CT scan</a>

773 (CAT scan)</strong>

774: A procedure that makes a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, such as the neck, chest, abdomen, and pelvis, taken from different angles. The pictures are made by a computer linked to an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

775x-ray</a>

776 machine. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000409764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

777dye</a>

778 may be <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

779injected</a>

780 into a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

781vein</a>

782 or swallowed to help the organs or tissues show up more clearly. This procedure is also called computed tomography, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44236&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044236&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

783computerized tomography</a>

784, or computerized axial tomography.<figure id="figure_423" class="image-center">

785<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/775531.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

786Enlarge</a>

787<img id="_423" alt="Computed tomography (CT) scan; drawing shows a child lying on a table that slides through the CT scanner, which takes a series of detailed x-ray pictures of areas inside the body." title="Computed tomography (CT) scan; drawing shows a child lying on a table that slides through the CT scanner, which takes a series of detailed x-ray pictures of areas inside the body." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/775531-750.jpg">

788<figcaption class="caption-container">

789Computed tomography (CT) scan. The child lies on a table that slides through the CT scanner, which takes a series of detailed x-ray pictures of areas inside the body.</figcaption>

790</figure>

791</li>

792<li>

793<strong>

794<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46140&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046140&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

795PET scan</a>

796 (positron emission tomography scan)</strong>

797: A procedure to find <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45772&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045772&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

798malignant</a>

799 tumor cells in the body. A small amount of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

800radioactive</a>

801 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044033&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

802glucose</a>

803 (sugar) is injected into a vein. The PET <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=386220&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000386220&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

804scanner</a>

805 rotates around the body and makes a picture of where glucose is being used in the body. Malignant tumor cells show up brighter in the picture because they are more active and take up more glucose than normal cells do. Sometimes a PET scan and a CT scan are done at the same time. If there is any cancer, this increases the chance that it will be found.<figure id="figure_424" class="image-center">

806<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/775456.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

807Enlarge</a>

808<img id="_424" alt="Positron emission tomography (PET) scan; drawing shows a child lying on table that slides through the PET scanner." title="Positron emission tomography (PET) scan; drawing shows a child lying on table that slides through the PET scanner." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/775456-750.jpg">

809<figcaption class="caption-container">

810Positron emission tomography (PET) scan. The child lies on a table that slides through the PET scanner. The head rest and white strap help the child lie still. A small amount of radioactive glucose (sugar) is injected into the child's vein, and a scanner makes a picture of where the glucose is being used in the body. Cancer cells show up brighter in the picture because they take up more glucose than normal cells do. </figcaption>

811</figure>

812</li>

813<li>

814<strong>

815<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045788&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

816MRI</a>

817 (magnetic resonance imaging)</strong>

818: A procedure that uses a magnet, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651209&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

819radio waves</a>

820, and a computer to make a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body. This procedure is also called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

821nuclear magnetic resonance imaging</a>

822 (NMRI).<figure id="figure_426" class="image-center">

828</figure>

829</li>

830<li>

831<strong>

832<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46303&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046303&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

833Lumbar puncture</a>

834</strong>

835: A procedure used to collect <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

836cerebrospinal fluid</a>

837 (CSF) from the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=396787&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000396787&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

838spinal column</a>

839. This is done by placing a needle between two bones in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=415914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000415914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

840spine</a>

841 and into the CSF around the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=340937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000340937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

842spinal cord</a>

843 and removing a sample of the fluid. The sample of CSF is checked under a microscope for signs that the cancer has spread to the brain and spinal cord. This procedure is also called an LP or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46592&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046592&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

844spinal tap</a>

845.<figure id="figure_278" class="image-center">

852</li>

853<li>

854<strong>

855<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=304687&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000304687&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

856Chest x-ray</a>

857</strong>

858: An x-ray of the organs and bones inside the chest. An x-ray is a type of energy beam that can go through the body and onto film, making a picture of areas inside the body.</li>

859<li>

860<strong>

861<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46157&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046157&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

862Ultrasound</a>

863 exam</strong>

864: A procedure in which high-energy sound waves (ultrasound) are bounced off internal tissues or organs and make echoes. The echoes form a picture of body tissues called a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46587&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046587&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

877<section id="_437">

878<h3 id="_438" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

879A biopsy is done to diagnose childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma.</h3>

880<p id="_439" tabindex="-1">

881Cells and tissues are removed during a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45164&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045164&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

882biopsy</a>

883 so they can be viewed under a microscope by a pathologist to check for cancer cells. Because treatment depends on the type of non-Hodgkin lymphoma, biopsy samples should be checked by a pathologist who has experience in diagnosing childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma. </p>

884<p id="_445" tabindex="-1">

885One of the following types of biopsies may be done:</p>

886<div class="pdq-content-list">

887<ul id="_440">

888<li>

889<strong>

890<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46411&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046411&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

891Excisional

892 biopsy</a>

893</strong>

894: The removal of an entire lymph node or lump of tissue. </li>

895<li>

896<strong>

897<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46698&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046698&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

898Incisional

899 biopsy</a>

900</strong>

901: The removal of part of a lump, lymph node, or sample of tissue.</li>

902<li>

903<strong>

904<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=641799&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000641799&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

905Core needle biopsy</a>

906</strong>

907: The removal of tissue or part of a lymph node using a wide needle.</li>

908<li>

909<strong>

910<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45691&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045691&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

911Fine-needle aspiration (FNA) biopsy</a>

912</strong>

913:

914 The removal of tissue or part of a lymph node using a thin needle.</li>

915</ul>

916</div>

917<p id="_441" tabindex="-1">

918The procedure used to remove the sample of tissue depends on where the tumor is in the body:</p>

919<div class="pdq-content-list">

920<ul id="_442">

921<li>

922<strong>

923<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46505&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046505&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

924Bone marrow aspiration</a>

925 and biopsy</strong>

926: The removal of bone marrow and a small piece of bone by inserting a hollow needle into the hipbone or breastbone.<figure id="figure_425" class="image-center">

927<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/775458.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

928Enlarge</a>

929<img id="_425" alt="Bone marrow aspiration and biopsy; drawing shows a child lying face down on a table and a bone marrow needle being inserted into the right hip bone. An inset shows the bone marrow needle being inserted through the skin into the bone marrow of the hip bone." title="Bone marrow aspiration and biopsy; drawing shows a child lying face down on a table and a bone marrow needle being inserted into the right hip bone. An inset shows the bone marrow needle being inserted through the skin into the bone marrow of the hip bone." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/775458-750.jpg">

930<figcaption class="caption-container">

931Bone marrow aspiration and biopsy. After a small area of skin is numbed, a bone marrow needle is inserted into the child&#8217;s hip bone. Samples of blood, bone, and bone marrow are removed for examination under a microscope.</figcaption>

932</figure>

933</li>

934<li>

935<strong>

936<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46287&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046287&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

937Mediastinoscopy</a>

938</strong>

939: A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

940surgical</a>

941 procedure to look at the organs, tissues, and lymph nodes between the lungs for <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

942abnormal</a>

943 areas. An <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46353&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046353&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

944incision</a>

945 (cut) is made at the top of the breastbone and a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=514453&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000514453&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

946mediastinoscope</a>

947 is inserted into the chest. A mediastinoscope is a thin, tube-like instrument with a light and a lens for viewing. It also has a tool to remove tissue or lymph node samples, which are checked under a microscope for signs of cancer.</li>

948<li>

949<strong>

950<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46533&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046533&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

951Anterior mediastinotomy</a>

952</strong>

953: A surgical procedure to look at the organs and tissues between the lungs and between the breastbone and heart for abnormal areas. An incision (cut) is made next to the breastbone and a mediastinoscope is inserted into the chest. A mediastinoscope is a thin, tube-like instrument with a light and a lens for viewing. It also has a tool to remove tissue or lymph node samples, which are checked under a microscope for signs of cancer. This is also called the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44370&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044370&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

954Chamberlain procedure</a>

955.</li>

956<li>

957<strong>

958<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46612&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046612&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

959Thoracentesis</a>

960</strong>

961: The removal of fluid from the space between the lining of the chest and the lung, using a needle. A pathologist views the fluid under a microscope to look for cancer cells.</li>

962</ul>

963</div>

964<p id="_443" tabindex="-1">

965If cancer is found, the following tests may be done to study the cancer cells:

966

967</p>

968<div class="pdq-content-list">

969<ul id="_444">

970<li>

971<strong>

972<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=653117&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000653117&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

973Immunohistochemistry</a>

974</strong>

975: A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46590&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046590&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

976laboratory test</a>

977 that uses antibodies to check for certain <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46086&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046086&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

978antigens</a>

979 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45776&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045776&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

980markers</a>

981) in a sample of a patient&#8217;s tissue. The antibodies are usually linked to an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46081&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046081&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

982enzyme</a>

983 or a fluorescent dye. After the antibodies bind to a specific antigen in the tissue sample, the enzyme or dye is activated, and the antigen can then be seen under a microscope. This type of test is used to help diagnose cancer and to help tell one type of cancer from another type of cancer.</li>

984<li>

985<strong>

986<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=335066&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000335066&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

987Flow cytometry</a>

988</strong>

989: A laboratory test that measures the number of cells in a sample, the percentage of live cells in a sample, and certain characteristics of the cells, such as size, shape, and the presence of tumor (or other) <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

990markers</a>

991 on the cell surface. The cells from a sample of a patient&#8217;s blood, bone marrow, or other tissue are stained with a fluorescent dye, placed in a fluid, and then passed one at a time through a beam of light. The test results are based on how the cells that were stained with the fluorescent dye react to the beam of light. This test is used to help diagnose and manage certain types of cancers, such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45343&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045343&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

992leukemia</a>

993 and lymphoma.</li>

994<li>

995<strong>

996<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270737&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270737&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

997Cytogenetic</a>

998 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=390238&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000390238&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

999analysis</a>

1000</strong>

1001: A laboratory test in which the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46470&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046470&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1002chromosomes</a>

1003 of cells in a sample of blood or bone marrow are counted and checked for any changes, such as broken, missing, rearranged, or extra chromosomes. Changes in certain chromosomes may be a sign of cancer. Cytogenetic analysis is used to help diagnose cancer, plan treatment, or find out how well treatment is working.</li>

1004<li>

1005<strong>

1006<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=460228&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000460228&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1007FISH</a>

1008 (fluorescence in situ hybridization)</strong>

1009: A laboratory test used to look at and count genes or chromosomes in cells and tissues. Pieces of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1010DNA</a>

1011 that contain fluorescent dyes are made in the laboratory and added to a sample of a patient&#8217;s cells or tissues. When these dyed pieces of DNA attach to certain genes or areas of chromosomes in the sample, they light up when viewed under a fluorescent microscope. The FISH test is used to help diagnose cancer and help plan treatment.</li>

1012<li>

1013<strong>

1014<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=341450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000341450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1015Immunophenotyping</a>

1016</strong>

1017: A laboratory test that uses antibodies to identify cancer cells based on the types of antigens or markers on the surface of the cells. This test is used to help diagnose specific types of lymphoma.</li>

1018</ul>

1019</div>

1020</section>

1021<section id="_22">

1022<h3 id="_23" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1023Certain factors affect prognosis (chance

1024 of recovery) and treatment options.</h3>

1025<p id="_140" tabindex="-1">

1026The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1027prognosis</a>

1028 and treatment options depend on:</p>

1029<div class="pdq-content-list">

1030<ul id="_141">

1031<li>

1032The type of lymphoma.</li>

1033<li>

1034Where the tumor is in the body when the tumor is diagnosed.</li>

1035<li>

1036The

1037 stage of the cancer.</li>

1038<li>

1039Whether there are certain changes in the chromosomes.</li>

1040<li>

1041The type of initial treatment.</li>

1042<li>

1043Whether the lymphoma responded to initial treatment.</li>

1044<li>

1045The patient&#8217;s age and general health.</li>

1046</ul>

1047</div>

1055 <h3>

1056Stages of Childhood Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma</h3>

1057

1058 <div id="_25" class="pdq-sections">

1059

1060 <div id="_section_25" class="pdq-sections">

1061<div class="key-points">

1062<h3 id="_25_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1063Key Points</h3>

1064<div id="_kp_section_25_2">

1065<ul>

1066<li>

1067After childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma has been diagnosed,

1068 tests are done to find out if cancer cells have spread within the lymph system

1069 or to other parts of the body. </li>

1070<li>

1071There are three ways that cancer spreads in the body.</li>

1072<li>

1073The following stages are used for childhood non-Hodgkin

1074 lymphoma:<ul>

1075<li>

1076Stage I</li>

1077<li>

1078Stage II</li>

1079<li>

1080Stage III</li>

1081<li>

1082Stage IV</li>

1083</ul>

1084</li>

1085<li>

1086Sometimes childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma does not respond to treatment or recurs (comes back) after treatment.</li>

1087</ul>

1088</div>

1089</div>

1090<section id="_26">

1091<h3 id="_27" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1092After childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma has been diagnosed,

1093 tests are done to find out if cancer cells have spread within the lymph system

1094 or to other parts of the body. </h3>

1095<p id="_28" tabindex="-1">

1096The process used to find out if <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1097cancer</a>

1098 has spread within the

1099 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1100lymph system</a>

1101 or to other parts of

1102 the body is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46597&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046597&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1103staging</a>

1104. The results of tests and procedures used to <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1105diagnose</a>

1106 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1107non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1108 may also be used for staging. The

1109 information gathered from the staging process determines the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1110stage</a>

1111 of the

1112 disease. It is important to know the stage in order to plan treatment.

1113 </p>

1114<p id="_851" tabindex="-1">

1115For a description of the tests and procedures used to diagnose non-Hodgkin lymphoma, see <a href="/types/lymphoma/patient/child-nhl-treatment-pdq#_19">

1116General Information</a>

1117.</p>

1118</section>

1119<section id="_205">

1120<h3 id="_206" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1121There are three ways that cancer spreads in the body.</h3>

1122<p id="_205_md_69" tabindex="-1">

1123Cancer can spread through <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1124tissue</a>

1125, the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1126lymph system</a>

1127, and the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1128blood</a>

1129:</p>

1130<div class="pdq-content-list">

1131<ul id="_205_md_70">

1132<li>

1133Tissue. The cancer spreads from where it began by growing into nearby areas.

1134</li>

1135<li>

1136Lymph system. The cancer spreads from where it began by getting into the lymph system. The cancer travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1137lymph vessels</a>

1138 to other parts of the body.

1139</li>

1140<li>

1141Blood. The cancer spreads from where it began by getting into the blood. The cancer travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1142blood vessels</a>

1143 to other parts of the body.

1144</li>

1145</ul>

1146</div>

1147</section>
