1149<h3 id="_31" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1150The following stages are used for childhood non-Hodgkin

1151 lymphoma:</h3>

1152<section id="_32">

1153<h4 id="_33" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1154Stage I</h4>

1155<figure id="figure_225" class="image-center">

1156<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/614610.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1157Enlarge</a>

1158<img id="_225" alt="Stage I childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma; drawing shows cancer in one group of lymph nodes. An inset shows a lymph node with a lymph vessel, an artery, and a vein. Lymphoma cells containing cancer are shown in the lymph node." title="Stage I childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma; drawing shows cancer in one group of lymph nodes. An inset shows a lymph node with a lymph vessel, an artery, and a vein. Lymphoma cells containing cancer are shown in the lymph node." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/614610-750.jpg">

1159<figcaption class="caption-container">

1160Stage I childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma. Cancer is found in one group of lymph nodes or one area outside the lymph nodes, but no cancer is found in the abdomen or mediastinum (area between the lungs).</figcaption>

1161</figure>

1162<p id="_217" tabindex="-1">

1163In <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=330108&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000330108&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1164stage I childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1165, cancer is found:</p>

1166<div class="pdq-content-list">

1167<ul id="_222">

1168<li>

1169in one group of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1170lymph nodes</a>

1171; or</li>

1172<li>

1173in one area outside the lymph nodes.</li>

1174</ul>

1175</div>

1176<p id="_223" tabindex="-1">

1177No cancer is found in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1178abdomen</a>

1179 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46288&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046288&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1180mediastinum</a>

1181 (area between the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1182lungs</a>

1183).</p>

1184</section>

1185<section id="_35">

1186<h4 id="_36" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1187Stage II</h4>

1188<figure id="figure_226" class="image-center">

1189<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/633800.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1190Enlarge</a>

1191<img id="_226" alt="Stage II childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma; drawing shows cancer in lymph node groups above and below the diaphragm, in the liver, and in the appendix. The colon and small intestine are also shown. An inset shows a lymph node with a lymph vessel, an artery, and a vein. Lymphoma cells containing cancer are shown in the lymph node." title="Stage II childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma; drawing shows cancer in lymph node groups above and below the diaphragm, in the liver, and in the appendix. The colon and small intestine are also shown. An inset shows a lymph node with a lymph vessel, an artery, and a vein. Lymphoma cells containing cancer are shown in the lymph node." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/633800-750.jpg">

1192<figcaption class="caption-container">

1193Stage II childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma. Cancer is found in one area outside the lymph nodes and in nearby lymph nodes (a); or in two or more areas above (b) or below (c) the diaphragm; or cancer started in the stomach, appendix, or intestines (d) and can be removed by surgery. </figcaption>

1194</figure>

1195<p id="_37" tabindex="-1">

1196In <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=330109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000330109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1197stage II childhood non-Hodgkin

1198 lymphoma</a>

1199, cancer is found:</p>

1200<div class="pdq-content-list">

1201<ul id="_219">

1202<li>

1203in one area outside the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1204lymph nodes</a>

1205 and in nearby lymph nodes; or</li>

1206<li>

1207in two or more areas either above or below the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46451&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046451&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1208diaphragm</a>

1209, and may have spread to nearby lymph nodes; or</li>

1210<li>

1211to have started in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46604&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046604&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1212stomach</a>

1213 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46335&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046335&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1214intestines</a>

1215 and can be completely removed by <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1216surgery</a>

1217. Cancer may have spread to certain nearby lymph nodes.</li>

1218</ul>

1231<p id="_41" tabindex="-1">

1232In <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=330110&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000330110&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1234 childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1236<div class="pdq-content-list">

1238<li>

1239in at least one area above the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46451&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046451&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1240diaphragm</a>

1241 and in at least one area below the diaphragm; or</li>

1242<li>

1243to have started in the chest; or</li>

1244<li>

1245to have started in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1246abdomen</a>

1247 and spread throughout the abdomen and cannot be completely removed by <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1248surgery</a>

1249; or</li>

1250<li>

1251in the area around the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=415914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000415914&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1253.</li>

1267<p id="_45" tabindex="-1">

1268In <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=330112&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000330112&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1270 non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1272bone marrow</a>

1273, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=797669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000797669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1274brain</a>

1275, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1276cerebrospinal fluid</a>

1277. Cancer may also be found in other parts of the body.</p>

1280<section id="_477">

1281<h3 id="_478" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1282Sometimes childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma does not respond to treatment or recurs (comes back) after treatment.</h3>

1283<p id="_838" tabindex="-1">

1284<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=350245&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000350245&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1285Refractory</a>

1286 non-Hodgkin lymphoma is cancer that does not respond to initial treatment.</p>

1287<p id="_479" tabindex="-1">

1288<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45862&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045862&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1289Recurrent</a>

1290 non-Hodgkin lymphoma is cancer that has come back after treatment. It may come

1291 back in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1292lymph system</a>

1293 or in other parts of the body. </p>

1294</section>

1301 <h3>

1302Treatment Option Overview</h3>

1303

1304 <div id="_48" class="pdq-sections">

1305

1306 <div id="_section_48" class="pdq-sections">

1307<div class="key-points">

1308<h3 id="_48_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1309Key Points</h3>

1310<div id="_kp_section_48_3">

1311<ul>

1312<li>

1313There are different types of treatment for children with

1314 non-Hodgkin lymphoma. </li>

1315<li>

1316Children with non-Hodgkin lymphoma should have their

1317 treatment planned by a team of doctors who are experts in treating childhood

1318 cancer.</li>

1319<li>

1320Eight types of treatment are used:<ul>

1321<li>

1322Surgery</li>

1323<li>

1324Chemotherapy</li>

1325<li>

1326Radiation therapy</li>

1327<li>

1328High-dose chemotherapy with stem cell transplant</li>

1329<li>

1330Targeted therapy</li>

1331<li>

1332Other drug therapy</li>

1333<li>

1334Phototherapy</li>

1335<li>

1336Watchful waiting</li>

1337</ul>

1338</li>

1339<li>

1340New types of treatment are being tested in clinical

1341 trials. <ul>

1342<li>

1343Immunotherapy</li>

1344<li>

1345Treatment for childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma may cause side effects.</li>

1346</ul>

1347</li>

1348<li>

1349Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial.</li>

1350<li>

1351Patients can enter clinical trials before, during, or after starting their cancer treatment.</li>

1352<li>

1353Follow-up tests may be needed.</li>

1354</ul>

1355</div>

1356</div>

1357<section id="_49">

1358<h3 id="_50" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1359There are different types of treatment for children with

1360 non-Hodgkin lymphoma. </h3>

1361<p id="_51" tabindex="-1">

1362Different types of treatment are available for children with

1363 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045148&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1364non-Hodgkin lymphoma</a>

1365. Some

1366 treatments are <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1367standard</a>

1368 (the currently used treatment), and some are being

1369 tested in <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1370clinical trials</a>

1371. A treatment clinical trial is a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651211&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651211&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1372research study</a>

1373 meant to help improve

1374 current treatments or obtain information on new treatments for patients with

1375 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1376cancer</a>

1377. When clinical trials show that a new treatment is better than the

1378 standard treatment, the new

1379 treatment may become the standard treatment. </p>

1380<p id="_52" tabindex="-1">

1381Taking part in a clinical trial

1382 should be considered for all children with non-Hodgkin lymphoma. Some clinical trials are open only to patients who have not started treatment. </p>

1383</section>

1384<section id="_53">

1385<h3 id="_54" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1386Children with non-Hodgkin lymphoma should have their

1387 treatment planned by a team of doctors who are experts in treating childhood

1388 cancer.</h3>

1389<p id="_55" tabindex="-1">

1390Treatment will be overseen by a

1391 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=693555&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000693555&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1392pediatric oncologist</a>

1393, a doctor who specializes

1394 in treating children with cancer. The pediatric oncologist works with other <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=650566&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000650566&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1395health care providers</a>

1396 who are experts in treating children

1397 with non-Hodgkin lymphoma and who specialize in certain areas of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=482419&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000482419&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1398medicine</a>

1399.

1400 These may include the following <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=478785&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000478785&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1402:</p>

1441<section id="_57">

1442<h3 id="_58" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1443Eight types of treatment are used:</h3>

1444<section id="_839">

1445<h4 id="_854" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1446Surgery</h4>

1447<p id="_840" tabindex="-1">

1448<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1449Surgery</a>

1450 may be done to remove as much of the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1451tumor</a>

1452 as possible for some types of childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma. After the doctor removes all the cancer that can be seen at the time of surgery, patients may be given <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45214&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045214&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1453chemotherapy</a>

1454 to kill any cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1455cells</a>

1456 that are left. Treatment given after the surgery, to lower the risk that the cancer will come back, is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45587&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045587&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1457adjuvant therapy</a>

1458.</p>

1459</section>

1460<section id="_59">

1461<h4 id="_60" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1462Chemotherapy</h4>

1463<p id="_112" tabindex="-1">

1464Chemotherapy is a cancer treatment that uses <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=348921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000348921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1465drugs</a>

1466 to stop the growth of cancer cells, either by killing the cells or by stopping them from dividing. When chemotherapy is taken by mouth or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044678&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1467injected</a>

1468 into a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1469vein</a>

1470 or muscle, the drugs enter the bloodstream and can reach cancer cells throughout the body (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45922&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045922&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1471systemic chemotherapy</a>

1472). When chemotherapy is placed directly into the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1473cerebrospinal fluid</a>

1474 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46681&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046681&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1475intrathecal chemotherapy</a>

1476), an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1477organ</a>

1478, or a body <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=463703&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000463703&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1479cavity</a>

1480 such as the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1481abdomen</a>

1482, the drugs mainly affect cancer cells in those areas. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45650&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045650&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1483Combination chemotherapy</a>

1484 is treatment using two or more anticancer drugs. </p>

1485<p id="_416" tabindex="-1">

1486Intrathecal chemotherapy may be used to treat

1487 childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma that has spread, or may spread, to the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=797669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000797669&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1488brain</a>

1489. When used to lessen the chance cancer will spread to the brain, it is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46472&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046472&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1490CNS prophylaxis</a>

1491. Intrathecal chemotherapy is given in addition to chemotherapy by mouth or vein.

1492

1493Higher than usual <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44664&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044664&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1494doses</a>

1495 of chemotherapy may also be used as CNS prophylaxis.</p>

1496<figure id="figure_215" class="image-center">

1497<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/539773.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1498Enlarge</a>

1499<img id="_215" alt="Intrathecal chemotherapy; drawing shows the cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) in the brain and spinal cord, and an Ommaya reservoir (a dome-shaped container that is placed under the scalp during surgery; it holds the drugs as they flow through a small tube into the brain). Top section shows a syringe and needle injecting anticancer drugs into the Ommaya reservoir. Bottom section shows a syringe and needle injecting anticancer drugs directly into the cerebrospinal fluid in the lower part of the spinal column." title="Intrathecal chemotherapy; drawing shows the cerebrospinal fluid (CSF) in the brain and spinal cord, and an Ommaya reservoir (a dome-shaped container that is placed under the scalp during surgery; it holds the drugs as they flow through a small tube into the brain). Top section shows a syringe and needle injecting anticancer drugs into the Ommaya reservoir. Bottom section shows a syringe and needle injecting anticancer drugs directly into the cerebrospinal fluid in the lower part of the spinal column." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/539773-750.jpg">

1500<figcaption class="caption-container">

1501Intrathecal chemotherapy. Anticancer drugs are injected into the intrathecal space, which is the space that holds the cerebrospinal fluid (CSF, shown in blue). There are two different ways to do this. One way, shown in the top part of the figure, is to inject the drugs into an Ommaya reservoir (a dome-shaped container that is placed under the scalp during surgery; it holds the drugs as they flow through a small tube into the brain). The other way, shown in the bottom part of the figure, is to inject the drugs directly into the CSF in the lower part of the spinal column, after a small area on the lower back is numbed. </figcaption>

1502</figure>

1503<p id="_450" tabindex="-1">

1504The way the chemotherapy is given depends on the type and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1505stage</a>

1506 of the cancer being treated.</p>

1507<p id="_253" tabindex="-1">

1508For more information, see <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/drugs/non-hodgkin" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/drugs/non-hodgkin">

1509Drugs Approved for Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma</a>

1510.</p>

1511</section>

1512<section id="_62">

1513<h4 id="_63" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1514Radiation therapy</h4>

1515<p id="_113" tabindex="-1">

1516<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44971&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044971&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1517Radiation therapy</a>

1518 is a cancer treatment that uses high energy <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1519x-rays</a>

1520 or other types of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1521radiation</a>

1522 to kill cancer cells or keep them from growing. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46686&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046686&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1523External radiation therapy</a>

1524 uses a machine outside the body to send radiation toward the area of the body with cancer. External radiation therapy may be used to treat childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma that has spread, or may spread, to the brain and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=340937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000340937&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1525spinal cord</a>

1526. External radiation therapy may also be used to treat <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46771&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046771&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1527cutaneous T-cell lymphoma</a>

1528 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45794&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045794&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1529mycosis fungoides</a>

1530).</p>

1531</section>

1532<section id="_67">

1533<h4 id="_68" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1534High-dose chemotherapy with stem cell transplant</h4>

1535<p id="_472" tabindex="-1">

1536<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=346522&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000346522&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1537High doses of chemotherapy</a>

1538 are given to kill cancer cells. Healthy cells, including <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1539blood</a>

1540-forming cells, are also destroyed by the cancer treatment. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46695&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046695&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1541Stem cell transplant</a>

1542 is a treatment to replace the blood-forming cells. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46598&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046598&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1543Stem cells</a>

1544 (immature blood cells) are removed from the blood or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1545bone marrow</a>

1546 of the patient or a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=643010&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000643010&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1547donor</a>

1548 and are frozen and stored. After the patient completes chemotherapy, the stored stem cells are thawed and given to the patient through an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45738&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045738&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1549infusion</a>

1550. These reinfused stem cells grow into (and restore) the body's blood cells.</p>

1551<p id="_254" tabindex="-1">

1552For more information, see <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/drugs/non-hodgkin" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/drugs/non-hodgkin">

1553Drugs Approved for Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma</a>

1554.</p>

1555<figure id="figure_279" class="image-center">

1556<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/765030.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1557Enlarge</a>

1558<img id="_279" alt="Stem cell transplant; (Panel 1): Drawing of stem cells being removed from a patient or donor. Blood is collected from a vein in the arm and flows through a machine that removes the stem cells; the remaining blood is returned to a vein in the other arm. (Panel 2): Drawing of a health care provider giving a patient treatment to kill blood-forming cells. Chemotherapy is given to the patient through a catheter in the chest. (Panel 3): Drawing of stem cells being given to the patient through a catheter in the chest." title="Stem cell transplant; (Panel 1): Drawing of stem cells being removed from a patient or donor. Blood is collected from a vein in the arm and flows through a machine that removes the stem cells; the remaining blood is returned to a vein in the other arm. (Panel 2): Drawing of a health care provider giving a patient treatment to kill blood-forming cells. Chemotherapy is given to the patient through a catheter in the chest. (Panel 3): Drawing of stem cells being given to the patient through a catheter in the chest." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/765030-750.jpg">

1559<figcaption class="caption-container">

1560Stem cell transplant. (Step 1): Blood is taken from a vein in the arm of the donor. The patient or another person may be the donor. The blood flows through a machine that removes the stem cells. Then the blood is returned to the donor through a vein in the other arm. (Step 2): The patient receives chemotherapy to kill blood-forming cells. The patient may receive radiation therapy (not shown). (Step 3): The patient receives stem cells through a catheter placed into a blood vessel in the chest.</figcaption>

1561</figure>

1563<section id="_245">

1564<h4 id="_246" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1565Targeted therapy</h4>

1566<p id="_247" tabindex="-1">

1567<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270742&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270742&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1568Targeted therapy</a>

1569 uses drugs or other substances to block the action of specific enzymes, proteins, or other molecules involved in the growth and spread of cancer cells. Types of targeted therapy include the following:</p>

1570<div class="pdq-content-list">

1571<ul id="_841">

1572<li>

1573<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46066&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046066&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1574Monoclonal antibody</a>

1575 therapy: Monoclonal antibodies are <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1576immune system</a>

1577 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1578proteins</a>

1579 made in the laboratory to treat many diseases, including cancer. As a cancer treatment, these antibodies can attach to a specific target on cancer cells or other cells that may help cancer cells grow. The antibodies are able to then kill the cancer cells, block their growth, or keep them from spreading. Monoclonal antibodies are given by infusion. They may be used alone or to carry drugs, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046622&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1580toxins</a>

1581, or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1582radioactive</a>

1583 material directly to cancer cells. Monoclonal antibodies may be used in combination with chemotherapy as adjuvant therapy.<p id="_842" tabindex="-1">

1584Types of monoclonal antibodies include: </p>

1708<h4 id="_452" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1709Phototherapy</h4>

1710<p id="_453" tabindex="-1">

1711<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=589410&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000589410&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1712Phototherapy</a>

1713 is a cancer treatment that uses a drug and a certain type of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45748&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045748&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1714laser</a>

1715 light to kill cancer cells. A drug that is not active until it is exposed to light is injected into a vein. The drug collects more in cancer cells than in normal cells. For <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=445084&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000445084&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1716skin cancer</a>

1717 in the skin, laser light is shined onto the skin and the drug becomes active and kills the cancer cells. Phototherapy is used in the treatment of cutaneous T-cell lymphoma.</p>

1744<section id="_473">

1745<h4 id="_474" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1746Immunotherapy</h4>

1747<p id="_475" tabindex="-1">

1748<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45729&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045729&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1749Immunotherapy</a>

1750 helps a person's immune system fight cancer. Types of immunotherapy include:</p>

1751<div class="pdq-content-list">

1752<ul id="_834">

1753<li>

1754<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=771302&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000771302&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1755CAR T-cell therapy</a>

1756: This treatment changes the patient's <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1757T cells</a>

1758 (a type of immune system cell) so they will attack certain proteins on the surface of cancer cells. T cells are taken from the patient and special <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44958&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044958&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1759receptors</a>

1760 are added to their surface in the laboratory. The changed cells are called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=787969&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000787969&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1761chimeric antigen receptor</a>

1762 (CAR) T cells. The CAR T cells are grown in the laboratory and given to the patient by infusion. The CAR T cells multiply in the patient's blood and attack cancer cells. CAR T-cell therapy is being studied in the treatment of Burkitt lymphoma/leukemia and diffuse large B-cell lymphoma that has not responded to treatment or has recurred (come back).<figure id="figure_835" class="image-center">

1763<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/774647.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1764Enlarge</a>

1765<img id="_835" alt="CAR T-cell therapy; drawing of blood being removed from a vein in a patient&#8217;s arm to get T cells. Also shown is a special receptor called a chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) being made in the laboratory; the gene for CAR is inserted into the T cells and then millions of CAR T cells are grown. Drawing also shows the CAR T cells being given to the patient by infusion and binding to antigens on the cancer cells and killing them." title="CAR T-cell therapy; drawing of blood being removed from a vein in a patient&#8217;s arm to get T cells. Also shown is a special receptor called a chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) being made in the laboratory; the gene for CAR is inserted into the T cells and then millions of CAR T cells are grown. Drawing also shows the CAR T cells being given to the patient by infusion and binding to antigens on the cancer cells and killing them." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/774647-750.jpg">

1766<figcaption class="caption-container">

1767CAR T-cell therapy. A type of treatment in which a patient&#8217;s T cells (a type of immune cell) are changed in the laboratory so they will bind to cancer cells and kill them. Blood from a vein in the patient&#8217;s arm flows through a tube to an apheresis machine (not shown), which removes the white blood cells, including the T cells, and sends the rest of the blood back to the patient. Then, the gene for a special receptor called a chimeric antigen receptor (CAR) is inserted into the T cells in the laboratory. Millions of the CAR T cells are grown in the laboratory and then given to the patient by infusion. The CAR T cells are able to bind to an antigen on the cancer cells and kill them.</figcaption>

1768</figure>

1769</li>

1770<li>

1771<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45684&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045684&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1772Epstein-Barr virus</a>

1773 (EBV)-specific <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=634067&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000634067&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1774cytotoxic T-lymphocytes</a>

1775 are a type of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=797381&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000797381&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1776immune cell</a>

1777 that can kill certain cells, including foreign cells, cancer cells, and cells infected with the EBV. Cytotoxic T-lymphocytes can be separated from other blood cells, grown in the laboratory, and then given to the patient to kill cancer cells. EBV-specific cytotoxic T-lymphocytes are being studied to treat <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=468786&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000468786&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1778post-transplant lymphoproliferative disease</a>

1779.</li>

1780<li>

1781<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45187&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045187&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1782Cyclosporine A</a>

1783: This treatment is used in combination with steroids to treat subcutaneous panniculitic T-cell lymphoma. </li>

1784</ul>

1785</div>

1786</section>

1787<section id="_200">

1788<h4 id="_201" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1789Treatment for childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma may cause side effects.</h4>

1790<p id="_200_md_76" tabindex="-1">

1791For information about <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46580&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046580&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1792side effects</a>

1793 that begin during treatment for cancer, see our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/side-effects">

1794Side Effects</a>

1795 page.</p>

1796<p id="_202" tabindex="-1">

1797<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46580&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046580&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1798Side effects</a>

1799 from cancer treatment that begin after treatment and continue for months or years are called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=390292&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000390292&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1800late effects</a>

1801. Late effects of cancer treatment may include the following:

1802

1803</p>

1804<div class="pdq-content-list">

1805<ul id="_203">

1806<li>

1807Physical problems, including problems with the heart, bones, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46399&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046399&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1808fertility</a>

1809.</li>

1810<li>

1811Changes in mood, feelings, thinking, learning, or memory.</li>

1812<li>

1813<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46658&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046658&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1814Second cancers</a>

1815 (new types of cancer), such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=387264&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000387264&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1816brain tumors</a>

1817, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46347&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046347&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1818acute myeloid leukemia</a>

1819, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45266&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045266&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1820myelodysplastic syndrome</a>

1821. </li>

1822</ul>

1823</div>

1824<p id="_204" tabindex="-1">

1825Some late effects may be treated or controlled. It is important to talk with your child's doctors about the effects cancer treatment can have on your child. For more information, see <a href="/types/childhood-cancers/late-effects-pdq">

1826Late Effects of Treatment for Childhood Cancer</a>

1827.</p>

1828</section>

1829</section>

1830<section id="_207">

1831<h3 id="_208" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1832Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial.</h3>

1833<p id="_207_md_23" tabindex="-1">

1834For some patients, taking part in a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1835clinical trial</a>

1836 may be the best treatment choice. Clinical trials are part of the cancer research process. Clinical trials are done to find out if new cancer treatments are safe and effective or better than the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1837standard treatment</a>

1838.</p>

1839<p id="_207_md_24" tabindex="-1">

1840Many of today's standard treatments for cancer are based on earlier clinical trials. Patients who take part in a clinical trial may receive the standard treatment or be among the first to receive a new treatment.</p>

1841<p id="_207_md_25" tabindex="-1">

1842Patients who take part in clinical trials also help improve the way cancer will be treated in the future. Even when clinical trials do not lead to effective new treatments, they often answer important questions and help move research forward.</p>

1843</section>

1844<section id="_209">

1845<h3 id="_210" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1846Patients can enter clinical trials before, during, or after starting their cancer treatment.</h3>

1847<p id="_209_md_29" tabindex="-1">

1848Some clinical trials only include patients who have not yet received treatment. Other trials test treatments for patients whose cancer has not gotten better. There are also clinical trials that test new ways to stop cancer from <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1849recurring</a>

1850 (coming back) or reduce the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46580&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046580&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1851side effects</a>

1852 of cancer treatment.</p>

1853<p id="_209_md_30" tabindex="-1">

1854Clinical trials are taking place in many parts of the country. Information about clinical trials supported by NCI can be found on NCI&#8217;s <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

1855clinical trials search</a>

1856 webpage. Clinical trials supported by other organizations can be found on the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

1857ClinicalTrials.gov</a>

1858 website.</p>

1859</section>

1860<section id="_211">

1861<h3 id="_212" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1862Follow-up tests may be needed.</h3>

1863<p id="_211_md_55" tabindex="-1">

1864Some of the tests that were done to <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1865diagnose</a>

1866 the cancer or to find out the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1867stage</a>

1868 of the cancer may be repeated. Some tests will be repeated in order to see how well the treatment is working. Decisions about whether to continue, change, or stop treatment may be based on the results of these tests.</p>

1869<p id="_211_md_56" tabindex="-1">

1870Some of the tests will continue to be done from time to time after treatment has ended. The results of these tests can show if your child's <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1871condition</a>

1872 has changed or if the cancer has <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1873recurred</a>

1874 (come back). These tests are sometimes called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044671&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1875follow-up</a>

1876 tests or check-ups.</p>

1877</section>

2989 <h3>

2990About This PDQ Summary</h3>

2991

2992 <div id="_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

2993

2994 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

2995<section id="_AboutThis_2">

2996<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

2997About PDQ</h3>

2998<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

2999Physician Data Query (PDQ) is the National Cancer Institute's (NCI's) comprehensive cancer information database. The PDQ database contains summaries of the latest published information on cancer prevention, detection, genetics, treatment, supportive care, and complementary and alternative medicine. Most summaries come in two versions. The health professional versions have detailed information written in technical language. The patient versions are written in easy-to-understand, nontechnical language. Both versions have cancer information that is accurate and up to date and most versions are also available in <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/espanol/publicaciones/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/espanol/publicaciones/pdq">

3000Spanish</a>

3001.</p>

3002<p id="_AboutThis_4" tabindex="-1">

3003PDQ is a service of the NCI. The NCI is part of the National Institutes of Health (NIH). NIH is the federal government&#8217;s center of biomedical research. The PDQ summaries are based on an independent review of the medical literature. They are not policy statements of the NCI or the NIH.</p>

3004</section>

3005<section id="_AboutThis_5">

3006<h3 id="_AboutThis_5_toc">

3007Purpose of This Summary</h3>

3008<p id="_AboutThis_6" tabindex="-1">

3009This PDQ cancer information summary has current information about the treatment of childhood non-Hodgkin lymphoma. It is meant to inform and help patients, families, and caregivers. It does not give formal guidelines or recommendations for making decisions about health care.</p>

3010</section>

3011<section id="_AboutThis_7">

3012<h3 id="_AboutThis_7_toc">

3013Reviewers and Updates</h3>

3014<p id="_AboutThis_8" tabindex="-1">

3015Editorial Boards write the PDQ cancer information summaries and keep them up to date. These Boards are made up of experts in cancer treatment and other specialties related to cancer. The summaries are reviewed regularly and changes are made when there is new information. The date on each summary ("Updated") is the date of the most recent change.

3016</p>

3017<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

3018The information in this patient summary was taken from the health professional version, which is reviewed regularly and updated as needed, by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment">

3019PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board</a>

3020.

3021</p>

3022</section>

3023<section id="_AboutThis_10">

3024<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

3025Clinical Trial Information</h3>

3026<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

3027A clinical trial is a study to answer a scientific question, such as whether one treatment is better than another. Trials are based on past studies and what has been learned in the laboratory. Each trial answers certain scientific questions in order to find new and better ways to help cancer patients. During treatment clinical trials, information is collected about the effects of a new treatment and how well it works. If a clinical trial shows that a new treatment is better than one currently being used, the new treatment may become "standard." Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial. Some clinical trials are open only to patients who have not started treatment.

3028</p>

3029<p id="_AboutThis_12" tabindex="-1">

3030Clinical trials can be found online at <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials">

3031NCI's website</a>

3032. For more information, call the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/contact-center" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/contact-center">

3033Cancer Information Service</a>

3034 (CIS), NCI's contact center, at 1-800-4-CANCER (1-800-422-6237).

3035</p>

3036</section>

3037<section id="_AboutThis_13">

3038<h3 id="_AboutThis_13_toc">

3039Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

3040<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

3041PDQ is a registered trademark. The content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text. It cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless the whole summary is shown and it is updated regularly. However, a user would be allowed to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks in the following way: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;

3042</p>

3043<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

3044The best way to cite this PDQ summary is:</p>

3045<p id="_AboutThis_21" tabindex="-1">

3046PDQ&#174; Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Childhood Non-Hodgkin Lymphoma Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/lymphoma/patient/child-nhl-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/lymphoma/patient/child-nhl-treatment-pdq">

3047https://www.cancer.gov/types/lymphoma/patient/child-nhl-treatment-pdq</a>

3048. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389294]</p>

3049<p id="_AboutThis_16" tabindex="-1">

3050Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use in the PDQ summaries only. If you want to use an image from a PDQ summary and you are not using the whole summary, you must get permission from the owner. It cannot be given by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the images in this summary, along with many other images related to cancer can be found in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

3051Visuals Online</a>

3052. Visuals Online is a collection of more than 3,000 scientific images.

3053</p>
